‚Źļ Created /workflow. This is the master command ‚ÄĒ it runs the full pipeline:

PLAN ‚Üí SCAFFOLD ‚Üí BUILD ‚Üí TEST ‚Üí REVIEW ‚Üí AUDIT ‚Üí PUSH

Key design decisions:

- Hard gates ‚ÄĒ can't proceed to BUILD until the plan is approved, can't PUSH if there are blockers
- Skippable stages ‚ÄĒ tiny fixes skip PLAN/SCAFFOLD/TEST, bug fixes skip SCAFFOLD
- Session tracking ‚ÄĒ shows a running checklist so you always know where you are
- Self-contained ‚ÄĒ doesn't call other slash commands, it IS the pipeline (avoids confusion with duplicate /plan etc.)

Final suite ‚ÄĒ 11 commands:

‚ĒĆ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚Ē¨‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚Ēź

‚Źļ Good question. Here's the split:

phases/phase_1_plan.md ‚ÄĒ The what and status

- Checklist of every task in the phase
- Check marks as features get completed
- Which step of the pipeline each feature is at
- Blockers, decisions made, scope changes
- The living tracker you look at to know "where are we"

docs/logs.md ‚ÄĒ The how and why

- Every action taken, with teaching notes
- Commands run, errors hit, fixes applied
- What was learned (Laravel patterns, gotchas)
- The history a future session reads to pick up context

Think of it as: plan = project manager's board, logs = engineer's notebook.

You create the phase_1_plan.md, I'll update it as I complete tasks and keep logging the detail in logs.md. They reference each other but don't duplicate.

‚ĚĮ I'll name it Phase 1

‚Źļ Got it. phases/phase1.md ‚ÄĒ you create it, I'll update it as I work through the pipeline.

Testing out feaure 2-
First make sure the server is running:

php -d error_reporting=0 artisan serve

Then login at http://127.0.0.1:8000 with admin / 123456.

Manual Test Checklist

1. Training List (Calendar View)

- Go to /staff/trainings
- You should see a calendar grid (Jan-Dec) with existing trainings
- Use the << and >> arrows to navigate years (try 2017 ‚ÄĒ that's where the existing data is)

2. Add a Training

- Click "Add More" button
- Fill in: Name, Provider, Description, Month, Year
- Check the "This training is mandatory" checkbox
- Set Expiry to 12 months
- Submit ‚ÄĒ should redirect back with success message
- The new training should appear in the correct month cell with a red "Required" badge

3. Edit a Training

- Click the pencil icon on any training
- Modal opens in read-only mode (fields disabled)
- Click the pencil icon in the modal header to enable editing
- Change a field, submit ‚ÄĒ should save

4. Delete a Training

- Click pencil icon to open edit modal
- Click the trash icon ‚ÄĒ confirm dialog appears
- Confirm ‚ÄĒ training disappears (soft-deleted)

5. View Training Detail

- Click a training name link
- Should show: training name, mandatory badge (if set), expiry info
- Three sections: Active Staff, Completed, Not Completed

6. Assign Staff

- On the detail page, use the "Select Staff" dropdown
- Pick one or more staff members, click the + button
- Should show success message with count
- Try assigning the same staff again ‚ÄĒ should say "already assigned"

7. Update Staff Status

- On Active staff, click the cog icon ‚Üí "Mark complete"
- Staff should move to Completed section
- On Completed, the status should stick on page refresh

8. Multi-tenancy Check

- Try visiting /staff/training/view/999 (non-existent or other home's training)
- Should redirect to /staff/trainings with "Training not found"

9. Backend Admin View

- Login to the admin panel
- Go to /general-admin/staff/training
- Should list trainings with search and pagination
- Click the eye icon to view ‚ÄĒ should show staff breakdown

Here's your manual test checklist for Body Maps:

---

Manual Test Checklist ‚ÄĒ Feature 3: Body Maps

0. Setup

- Start server: php -d error_reporting=0 artisan serve
- Login as komal / 123456 (admin user, home_id 1)
- Direct URL: http://127.0.0.1:8000/service/body-map/7

1. Body Map Page Loads

- Go to /service/body-map/7
- You should see a full-body SVG diagram (front view + back view) with male and
  female outlines
- Existing injuries (25 records from 2018) should show as red highlighted regions
  on the body
- Back button (yellow arrow, top left) should link back to the service user profile

2. View Existing Injury Info

- Click on any red (active) body part
- "Injury Information" modal should open
- Should show a table with: Body Region, Type, Description, Date Discovered, Size,
  Colour, Recorded By, Date Recorded
- Old injuries (2018 data) will show "Not specified" / "None" for the new detail
  fields ‚ÄĒ that's expected
- Close the modal with the X or Close button

3. Add a New Injury

- Click on any empty (non-red) body part (e.g. a hand, a knee)
- "Injury Details" modal should open with a form
- Fill in:
    - Type: Select "Bruise" from dropdown
    - Description: "Small bruise on left knee from fall"
    - Date Discovered: Today's date (should be pre-filled)
    - Size: "2cm x 3cm"
    - Colour: "Purple"
- Click Save Injury
- Modal should close, the body part you clicked should now turn red
- Click that same red part again ‚ÄĒ info modal should show all the details you just
  entered

4. Add Injury Without Details (Minimum Fields)

- Click another empty body part
- Leave all fields blank (type, description, size, colour all optional)
- Click Save Injury
- Should succeed ‚ÄĒ the body part turns red
- Click it to view ‚ÄĒ should show "Not specified" / "None" for the empty fields

5. Add Injury With Each Type

- Test each injury type from the dropdown works:
    - Bruise, Wound, Rash, Burn, Swelling, Pressure Sore, Other
- Each should save successfully

6. Remove an Injury (Admin Only)

- Click a red body part (one you just added)
- Info modal opens ‚ÄĒ you should see a red "Remove Injury" button (bottom left of
  modal)
- Click it ‚ÄĒ confirmation dialog: "Are you sure you want to remove this injury?"
- Click OK ‚ÄĒ modal closes, body part goes back to empty (non-red)
- Refresh the page ‚ÄĒ the body part should still be empty (soft-deleted in DB)

7. Non-Admin Cannot Remove

- Login as a non-admin user (e.g. find a user with user_type = 'N' for home_id 1)
- Go to /service/body-map/7
- Click a red body part ‚ÄĒ info modal should open
- The "Remove Injury" button should NOT be visible ‚ÄĒ only a "Close" button
- If you somehow send the POST request (via dev tools), it should return 403

8. CSRF Protection

- Open browser Developer Tools ‚Üí Network tab
- Click an empty body part, fill in details, click Save
- In the Network tab, find the POST request to /service/body-map/injury/add
- Check Request Headers ‚ÄĒ should include X-CSRF-TOKEN header
- Check Response ‚ÄĒ should be JSON: {"success": true, "id": ..., "message": "Injury
  point added."}

9. Multi-tenancy Check

- Try visiting /service/body-map/999999 (non-existent risk)
- Should redirect back (risk assessment not found)
- If you have a risk_id from a different home, try that too ‚ÄĒ should also redirect

10. Back Body Parts Work

- Scroll down on the body map ‚ÄĒ there's a back view of the body (body parts with
  bck\_ IDs)
- Click an empty back body part ‚ÄĒ injury detail modal should open
- Save an injury ‚ÄĒ back body part should turn red
- Click it again ‚ÄĒ info modal should show details
- Same add/remove flow as front body parts

11. History Endpoint (Dev Tools)

- Open browser dev tools ‚Üí Console tab
- Run:
  fetch('/service/body-map/history/1').then(r=>r.json()).then(d=>console.log(d))
- Should return JSON with success: true and a data array containing all injuries
  (active + removed) for service_user_id 1
- Removed injuries should have is_deleted: "1"

12. Page Refresh Persistence

- Add 2-3 injuries on different body parts
- Refresh the page (F5)
- All the injuries you added should still be red (loaded from DB)
- Click each to verify the details persisted

13. Reaching Body Map Through the UI

- Go to a service user profile (try /service/user-profile/1)
- Find the Risk Assessment section
- Click the body map icon (human figure) next to a risk entry
- Should open the body map (either as a modal popup or full page depending on the
  view)

/careos-workflow Handover Notes ‚ÄĒ Feature 4 from Phase 1.

Details from phases/phase1.md:

What Exists:

- DB table: handover_log_book
- Model: NO dedicated model (uses raw DB)
- Controller: app/Http/Controllers/frontEnd/HandoverController.php ‚ÄĒ index() with search/date filtering, handover_log_edit()
- Routes: POST/GET /handover/daily/log, POST/GET /handover/daily/log/edit, POST /handover/service/log
- Views: resources/views/frontEnd/common/handover_logbook.blade.php, resources/views/frontEnd/serviceUserManagement/elements/handover_to_staff.blade.php

What's Missing (Build These):

- Create model: app/Models/HandoverLogBook.php with proper fillable, casts, relationships
- Create service: app/Services/HandoverService.php ‚ÄĒ move DB logic out of controller
- Verify/fix list view ‚ÄĒ ensure existing blade works, date order, search works
- Verify/fix create/edit form ‚ÄĒ shift info, key events, client updates, follow-up actions, priority flags
- Add staff-to-staff handover flow ‚ÄĒ outgoing shift writes notes, incoming shift acknowledges
- Server-side validation on all form inputs

Note: No CareRoster export exists ‚ÄĒ build from existing Laravel implementation and care home best practices.

‚úĽ Baked for 1m 18s ¬∑ 1 shell still running

‚ĚĮ [Image #2] is this a generic toast or a concerining onne  
 ‚éŅ [Image #2]

‚Źļ Generic Chrome warning ‚ÄĒ not concerning for your dev work.

That's Google Password Manager's "Password Checkup" feature. It cross-references passwords you save against a database of known leaked credentials from
public breaches (haveibeenpwned-style).

Why it fired: 123456 is literally the most common leaked password in the world ‚ÄĒ it appears in essentially every breach dataset. Chrome sees you used it,
checks its list, finds it, and warns you.

It does NOT mean:

- Your Care OS database was breached
- Someone leaked Omega Life credentials
- There's a security issue with the application

It just means: you used a trivially weak password that happens to exist in public breach lists (because millions of people have used 123456).

What to do: Click OK / dismiss. Don't let Chrome change it for you ‚ÄĒ this is a local dev password for a test account, not a real credential. The warning
is irrelevant in this context.

Also ‚ÄĒ login clearly worked. You're on /roster, seeing the Welcome dashboard with Active Clients, Quick Actions, etc. Ready to start testing Features 1‚Äď3
whenever you want.

‚Ä¶ +24 lines (ctrl+o to expand)

‚Źļ Found it ‚ÄĒ two issues:

1. Risk id 7 belongs to home_id 1, not home 8 (Aries House). Since komal's first home in her comma-separated list is 8, the index() method's check
   where('home_id', $homeId) fails and triggers redirect()->back()->with('error', 'Risk assessment not found').

2. The 404 you're seeing is the "back" redirect falling through ‚ÄĒ when there's no Referer header (e.g., you typed the URL directly), Laravel's
   redirect()->back() lands somewhere that doesn't exist. The error flash message is being eaten.

What to do

Navigate to body maps the proper way ‚ÄĒ through the Service User profile, not by typing a URL. That ensures you land on a risk that belongs to your home.
Walk-through:

1. Go to Service Users list (from sidebar)
2. Pick a service user that belongs to Aries House ‚ÄĒ looking at the DB, service user id 27 has several risks in home 8 (ids 149, 184, 185, 186)
3. Open their profile ‚Üí Risk Assessments ‚Üí Body Map (the popup view)

Or, to hit the full-page body map view directly, use one of komal's valid risk IDs:

http://127.0.0.1:8000/roster/service/body-map/149
http://127.0.0.1:8000/roster/service/body-map/184

These should load because home_id=8 matches.

Separate issue worth flagging

The controller's getHomeId() takes only the first home_id from the comma list (explode(',', $homeIds)[0]). That means if komal's current-session home is
Aries House (8) but her list starts with a different home, the check would fail even for risks she legitimately has access to. This is a bug pattern ‚ÄĒ
the check should be "is $homeId IN the user's comma list" and should use the currently selected home from the session, not [0]. I'd flag this for the
Feature 4 audit or a follow-up security pass.

Want to try /roster/service/body-map/149 in the browser and confirm the view loads?

‚úĽ Saut√©ed for 1m 4s ¬∑ 1 shell still running

‚ĚĮ how can i navigate to body map from the ui

Searched for 3 patterns (ctrl+o to expand)

‚Źļ Found it. Body Map is only reachable via the Service User Profile ‚Üí Risk Assessments flow, as a popup modal. Here's the path:

Navigation from the UI

1. Sidebar ‚Üí Service Users (or click "Service Users" in the main nav)
2. Click a service user to open their profile page
3. Scroll to (or click the tab for) Risk Assessments
4. Click on any existing risk assessment row ‚ÄĒ this opens a popup with risk details
5. In the popup's action buttons row, click the Body Map button ‚ÄĒ it shows as a person icon (fa fa-male) labeled "Body Map"
6. A #bodyMapModal opens with the full front/back body diagram

The button is hidden until you've opened a specific risk, because it binds su_risk_id dynamically via jQuery (see risk.blade.php:801-808).

Which service user to test with

Service user id 27 in Aries House has 4 risk assessments with existing body map data (risk ids 149, 184, 185, 186) ‚ÄĒ you already have 25+ existing
injuries in the DB for testing.

What to verify once you're in

- Front/Back toggle ‚ÄĒ switch between front and back body views
- Click an empty body part ‚ÄĒ the injury detail modal should open, capture type/description/date/size/colour
- Click an existing active body part ‚ÄĒ info modal shows recorded details + (if admin) a remove button
- Save an injury ‚ÄĒ should appear active on the map without page reload
- Remove an injury (admin only) ‚ÄĒ confirmation + removal
- History endpoint ‚ÄĒ check /roster/service/body-map/history/27 if there's a history link

If you can't find a service user in Aries House through the UI, let me know and I'll look up one with an actual name so you can search for them.

‚Źļ Got it ‚ÄĒ in Care OS's terminology, "Clients" = Service Users. They're listed under each care type (Residential, Domiciliary, Supported Living, Day
Centre) because a service user is tied to the home type they live in.

Path to Body Map

1. Sidebar ‚Üí Residential Care ‚Üí Clients (Aries House is a residential home, so this is the right section)
2. Click any client row to open their profile
3. Inside the profile, look for a tab/section called Risk Assessments (might be labelled "Risk & RMP", "Risks", "SU Risk", or just a tab in the profile's
   tabbed interface)
4. Click an existing risk assessment ‚ÄĒ a popup opens with risk details
5. In that popup, click the Body Map button (person icon, fa fa-male)
6. The body map modal opens

Client to look for

Service user id 27 in Aries House has 4 risk assessments with 25+ existing injuries on the body map ‚ÄĒ perfect for testing. Let me get their name so you
can find them in the Clients list.

What this means

1. The sidebar's "Clients" link goes to the new UI, which has hardcoded placeholder content (you can see "General Risk Assessment" with "Substance  
   misuse" text ‚ÄĒ that's dummy data, not tied to the su_risk table)
2. The Body Map feature we built, hardened, and shipped (Feature 3) is not reachable from the sidebar navigation. It lives in the legacy profile view
3. All those uncommitted security fixes are technically correct and tested ‚ÄĒ but no user would ever reach them through the current nav
4. The new UI is a rebuild-in-progress that's overriding the legacy UI in the sidebar but hasn't had any backend wiring done yet

How to reach Body Map RIGHT NOW

Bypass the sidebar and type the legacy profile URL directly:

http://127.0.0.1:8000/roster/service/user-profile/180

That'll load Alex Sheffield in the old profile page, where Risk Assessments actually work and the Body Map popup is functional.

Phase 1 implication (important)

This changes the scope conversation. If the client_details.blade.php rebuild is the future direction, then every Phase 1 feature we've "completed" may  
 need to be re-wired into the new UI (Incident Management, Staff Training, Body Maps). That's potentially a lot of additional work that isn't in
phases/phase1.md.

Before we proceed with Feature 4 (Handover Notes), I think we need to answer:

1. Is client_details.blade.php the future UI, or a side experiment?
2. If future: does Phase 1 need to include "wire features 1-3 into the new UI"?
3. If experiment: should the sidebar "Clients" link be pointed back at the legacy profile view so the hardened features are actually reachable?

This is a decision for you, not me. What do you know about how client_details.blade.php got there? Was it part of an earlier rebuild attempt, or did  
 someone on the team start it recently?

‚ĚĮ [Image #2] is this a generic toast or a concerining onne  
 ‚éŅ [Image #2]

‚Źļ Generic Chrome warning ‚ÄĒ not concerning for your dev work.

That's Google Password Manager's "Password Checkup" feature. It cross-references passwords you save against a database of known leaked credentials from
public breaches (haveibeenpwned-style).

Why it fired: 123456 is literally the most common leaked password in the world ‚ÄĒ it appears in essentially every breach dataset. Chrome sees you used it,
checks its list, finds it, and warns you.

It does NOT mean:

- Your Care OS database was breached
- Someone leaked Omega Life credentials
- There's a security issue with the application

It just means: you used a trivially weak password that happens to exist in public breach lists (because millions of people have used 123456).

What to do: Click OK / dismiss. Don't let Chrome change it for you ‚ÄĒ this is a local dev password for a test account, not a real credential. The warning
is irrelevant in this context.

Also ‚ÄĒ login clearly worked. You're on /roster, seeing the Welcome dashboard with Active Clients, Quick Actions, etc. Ready to start testing Features 1‚Äď3
whenever you want.

‚Ä¶ +24 lines (ctrl+o to expand)

‚Źļ Found it ‚ÄĒ two issues:

1. Risk id 7 belongs to home_id 1, not home 8 (Aries House). Since komal's first home in her comma-separated list is 8, the index() method's check
   where('home_id', $homeId) fails and triggers redirect()->back()->with('error', 'Risk assessment not found').

2. The 404 you're seeing is the "back" redirect falling through ‚ÄĒ when there's no Referer header (e.g., you typed the URL directly), Laravel's
   redirect()->back() lands somewhere that doesn't exist. The error flash message is being eaten.

What to do

Navigate to body maps the proper way ‚ÄĒ through the Service User profile, not by typing a URL. That ensures you land on a risk that belongs to your home.
Walk-through:

1. Go to Service Users list (from sidebar)
2. Pick a service user that belongs to Aries House ‚ÄĒ looking at the DB, service user id 27 has several risks in home 8 (ids 149, 184, 185, 186)
3. Open their profile ‚Üí Risk Assessments ‚Üí Body Map (the popup view)

Or, to hit the full-page body map view directly, use one of komal's valid risk IDs:

http://127.0.0.1:8000/roster/service/body-map/149
http://127.0.0.1:8000/roster/service/body-map/184

These should load because home_id=8 matches.

Separate issue worth flagging

The controller's getHomeId() takes only the first home_id from the comma list (explode(',', $homeIds)[0]). That means if komal's current-session home is
Aries House (8) but her list starts with a different home, the check would fail even for risks she legitimately has access to. This is a bug pattern ‚ÄĒ
the check should be "is $homeId IN the user's comma list" and should use the currently selected home from the session, not [0]. I'd flag this for the
Feature 4 audit or a follow-up security pass.

Want to try /roster/service/body-map/149 in the browser and confirm the view loads?

‚ĚĮ how can i navigate to body map from the ui

Searched for 3 patterns (ctrl+o to expand)

‚Źļ Found it. Body Map is only reachable via the Service User Profile ‚Üí Risk Assessments flow, as a popup modal. Here's the path:

Navigation from the UI

1. Sidebar ‚Üí Service Users (or click "Service Users" in the main nav)
2. Click a service user to open their profile page
3. Scroll to (or click the tab for) Risk Assessments
4. Click on any existing risk assessment row ‚ÄĒ this opens a popup with risk details
5. In the popup's action buttons row, click the Body Map button ‚ÄĒ it shows as a person icon (fa fa-male) labeled "Body Map"
6. A #bodyMapModal opens with the full front/back body diagram

The button is hidden until you've opened a specific risk, because it binds su_risk_id dynamically via jQuery (see risk.blade.php:801-808).

Which service user to test with

Service user id 27 in Aries House has 4 risk assessments with existing body map data (risk ids 149, 184, 185, 186) ‚ÄĒ you already have 25+ existing
injuries in the DB for testing.

What to verify once you're in

- Front/Back toggle ‚ÄĒ switch between front and back body views
- Click an empty body part ‚ÄĒ the injury detail modal should open, capture type/description/date/size/colour
- Click an existing active body part ‚ÄĒ info modal shows recorded details + (if admin) a remove button
- Save an injury ‚ÄĒ should appear active on the map without page reload
- Remove an injury (admin only) ‚ÄĒ confirmation + removal
- History endpoint ‚ÄĒ check /roster/service/body-map/history/27 if there's a history link

If you can't find a service user in Aries House through the UI, let me know and I'll look up one with an actual name so you can search for them.

‚Źļ Got it ‚ÄĒ in Care OS's terminology, "Clients" = Service Users. They're listed under each care type (Residential, Domiciliary, Supported Living, Day
Centre) because a service user is tied to the home type they live in.

Path to Body Map

1. Sidebar ‚Üí Residential Care ‚Üí Clients (Aries House is a residential home, so this is the right section)
2. Click any client row to open their profile
3. Inside the profile, look for a tab/section called Risk Assessments (might be labelled "Risk & RMP", "Risks", "SU Risk", or just a tab in the profile's
   tabbed interface)
4. Click an existing risk assessment ‚ÄĒ a popup opens with risk details
5. In that popup, click the Body Map button (person icon, fa fa-male)
6. The body map modal opens

Client to look for

Service user id 27 in Aries House has 4 risk assessments with 25+ existing injuries on the body map ‚ÄĒ perfect for testing. Let me get their name so you
can find them in the Clients list.

What this means

1. The sidebar's "Clients" link goes to the new UI, which has hardcoded placeholder content (you can see "General Risk Assessment" with "Substance
   misuse" text ‚ÄĒ that's dummy data, not tied to the su_risk table)
2. The Body Map feature we built, hardened, and shipped (Feature 3) is not reachable from the sidebar navigation. It lives in the legacy profile view
3. All those uncommitted security fixes are technically correct and tested ‚ÄĒ but no user would ever reach them through the current nav
4. The new UI is a rebuild-in-progress that's overriding the legacy UI in the sidebar but hasn't had any backend wiring done yet

How to reach Body Map RIGHT NOW

Bypass the sidebar and type the legacy profile URL directly:

http://127.0.0.1:8000/roster/service/user-profile/180

That'll load Alex Sheffield in the old profile page, where Risk Assessments actually work and the Body Map popup is functional.

Phase 1 implication (important)

This changes the scope conversation. If the client_details.blade.php rebuild is the future direction, then every Phase 1 feature we've "completed" may
need to be re-wired into the new UI (Incident Management, Staff Training, Body Maps). That's potentially a lot of additional work that isn't in
phases/phase1.md.

Before we proceed with Feature 4 (Handover Notes), I think we need to answer:

1. Is client_details.blade.php the future UI, or a side experiment?
2. If future: does Phase 1 need to include "wire features 1-3 into the new UI"?
3. If experiment: should the sidebar "Clients" link be pointed back at the legacy profile view so the hardened features are actually reachable?

This is a decision for you, not me. What do you know about how client_details.blade.php got there? Was it part of an earlier rebuild attempt, or did
someone on the team start it recently?

So:

- The legacy page you're looking at now (Alex Sheffield profile) is the real, mature UI that has existed since the project's first commit in March 2024  
  and has been evolved ever since
- The new client-details page with the CareRoster-style tabs was added just 7 days ago, on 2026-04-08, in a single bulk commit that brought over "all  
  pending dev work" ‚ÄĒ presumably from another branch or environment
- That new page is effectively a scaffold/mockup with hardcoded data ‚ÄĒ no backend wiring for Risk Assessments, no Body Map integration, no real client
  data

What this means practically

1. The Body Map feature we built, hardened, and shipped is still live and reachable ‚ÄĒ it just lives on the legacy profile page at  
   /service/user-profile/{id}, not through the new sidebar
2. The new client-details page is not our work ‚ÄĒ someone else (or an earlier session of you) scaffolded it to match the CareRoster React app's look,  
   probably as part of the larger rebuild direction the project is heading in
3. The sidebar links were switched to point at the new page (also in the 2026-04-08 commit), which made the legacy page effectively invisible unless you
   know the URL

Decision point for you

Before Feature 4 (Handover Notes), you need to decide:

Option A ‚ÄĒ Stay on legacy UI

- Build Feature 4 onto the existing legacy profile/views (same pattern as Features 1‚Äď3)
- The new client-details page becomes dead code
- Fastest path to Phase 1 completion
- Fix sidebar to point back at legacy URLs

Option B ‚ÄĒ Migrate to new UI

- Decide the client-details rebuild is the direction, wire up Features 1‚Äď3 into it
- Build Feature 4 in the new UI pattern
- Significant extra work, changes Phase 1 scope
- Need to know what other pages the 2026-04-08 commit introduced

Option C ‚ÄĒ Two-track (not recommended)

- Build Feature 4 on legacy, deal with the new UI later
- Technical debt keeps growing

My recommendation: Option A, plus fix the sidebar. The legacy views are working, tested, and secured. The new UI appears to be aspirational scaffolding ‚ÄĒ
not production code. Unless you know there's a plan (and timeline) to fully rebuild the frontend in that new style, don't let it block shipping actual  
 functional features.

But this is your call ‚ÄĒ do you know the story behind the 2026-04-08 commit? Who added client_details.blade.php and why?

‚Źļ Now I have the full picture. Here's your testing guide:

---

Feature 4: Handover Notes ‚ÄĒ Manual Testing Guide

Server: http://127.0.0.1:8000  
 Login: komal / 123456 / house Aries

There are two ways to access handover notes. Test both.

---

PATH A: View Handover Log Book (top menu)

Step 1: Open the Handover Log Book

1. Login and navigate to any page (e.g. Dashboard or Clients list)
2. Click the dropdown menu in the top-right corner (your user avatar/name)
3. You should see: Add User, Forms, General Admin, Lock, Hand Over, Log Out
4. Click "Hand Over"

What to check:

- A modal titled "Hand Over Log Book" opens
- It shows a "Logged" section with records grouped by date
- Each record shows: title, time, expand (+) button
- If no records exist, it should show "No Logs Found"

Step 2: Expand a record

1. Click the date header to expand records for that date
2. Click the green + icon on any record

What to check:

- The record expands showing: Details (textarea), Notes (textarea), Staff created (read-only), Handover Staff Name (read-only), Submit button
- An acknowledgment badge shows: either green "Acknowledged" or yellow "Pending" with a blue "Acknowledge" button

Step 3: Edit a record

1. Type something in the Details textarea
2. Type something in the Notes textarea
3. Click Submit

What to check:

- A green success message appears: "Record edited successfully"
- The message fades after ~5 seconds
- Close the modal, reopen Hand Over ‚ÄĒ your changes should persist

Step 4: Acknowledge a handover

1. Find a record with a yellow "Pending" badge
2. Click the blue "Acknowledge" button

What to check:

- Button changes to "Acknowledging..." and disables
- Badge changes from yellow "Pending" to green "Acknowledged"
- The Acknowledge button disappears
- Success message: "Handover acknowledged"
- Close and reopen ‚ÄĒ the record should still show "Acknowledged"

Step 5: Test search by title

1. In the Hand Over Log Book modal, find the Search section (if visible ‚ÄĒ there may be Logged/Search tabs)
2. Select type: Title
3. Type part of a record's title
4. Click Confirm

What to check:

- Results show only matching records
- "No records found" if nothing matches

Step 6: Test search by date

1. Change type to Date
2. Pick a date using the date picker
3. Click Confirm

What to check:

- Results filtered to that date
- Date picker opens and works correctly

---

PATH B: Handover from a Service User's Logbook

This is the flow where staff hand over a specific logbook entry to another staff member.

Step 7: Navigate to a service user's logbook

1. Go to Clients (sidebar) ‚Üí click View Details on any client
2. On the client details page, find the Log Book section/tab
3. You should see logbook entries for that client

Step 8: Hand over a logbook entry

1. On a logbook entry, look for an "Add to Handover" option (it may be in a dropdown/action menu on the entry)
2. Click it

What to check:

- A modal titled "Handover to Staff User" opens
- It shows a Select Staff User dropdown
- The dropdown is populated with staff from Aries home only (not staff from other homes)

Step 9: Complete the handover

1. Select a staff member from the dropdown
2. Click Submit

What to check:

- Success message: "Log has been handovered to staff member successfully"
- If you try the same staff member again ‚Üí "Log is already handovered to this staff member"

---

PATH C: Edge Cases & Security

Step 10: Empty state

1. If possible, find a home/context with no handover records
2. Open Hand Over from the top menu

What to check:

- Shows "No Logs Found" ‚ÄĒ not a blank page or error

Step 11: Special characters

1. Edit a handover record
2. In Details, type: <script>alert('test')</script> & "quotes" < > special chars
3. Submit, then close and reopen

What to check:

- The text appears exactly as typed (no alert popup!)
- Special characters display correctly, not as &amp; etc.

---

What to Report Back

For each step, note:

- PASS ‚ÄĒ works as described
- FAIL ‚ÄĒ describe what you saw instead
- BLOCKED ‚ÄĒ couldn't reach this step (describe why)
- MISSING ‚ÄĒ the UI element/button/tab doesn't exist on the page

The most critical things to verify:

1. Can you even find and open the Hand Over modal? (Step 1)
2. Do records load and display? (Step 2)
3. Does edit save and persist? (Step 3)
4. Does Acknowledge work? (Step 4)
5. Does the Handover to Staff flow work from a logbook entry? (Steps 7-9)

If Step 1 fails (modal doesn't open), everything else is blocked ‚ÄĒ report that immediately.

---

Total: 27 attack vectors, tested across 4 stages (TEST, REVIEW, AUDIT, PROD-READY).

The key shift: 14 of these are now verified by actually attacking via curl, not by reading code. The 3 vulnerabilities that slipped through in
Feature 4 (items 2, 3, 7) would all be caught now because REVIEW requires a failed exploit as proof, not a code pattern match.

‚úĽ Crunched for 39s

‚ĚĮ and what are the measures we are gonna take to ensure everything is production ready?

‚Źļ Based on what broke across 13 sessions and what the updated workflow now enforces:

---

Production Readiness Measures ‚ÄĒ Full List

1. Code Quality (enforced during BUILD, Stage 3)

‚Ēā 4d: Security ‚Ēā XSS strings, SQLi strings, missing CSRF, oversized input, wrong ‚Ēā Injection attacks, validation gaps ‚Ēā  
 ‚Ēā payloads ‚Ēā types ‚Ēā ‚Ēā  
 ‚Ēú‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚Ēľ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚Ēľ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚Ē§
‚Ēā 4e: Run all ‚Ēā php artisan test --filter=[Feature] ‚ÄĒ zero failures ‚Ēā No regressions ‚Ēā  
 ‚ĒĒ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚Ēī‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚Ēī‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚Ēė

3. Runtime Verification (Stage 5 ‚ÄĒ DEBUG)

‚ĒĆ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚Ē¨‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚Ē¨‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚Ēź  
 ‚Ēā Check ‚Ēā How ‚Ēā Catches ‚Ēā  
 ‚Ēú‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚Ēľ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚Ēľ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚Ē§  
 ‚Ēā Error log ‚Ēā Clear laravel.log ‚Üí hit every route ‚Üí check for new errors ‚Ēā PHP warnings, deprecations, undefined vars ‚Ēā  
 ‚Ēā clean ‚Ēā ‚Ēā ‚Ēā  
 ‚Ēú‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚Ēľ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚Ēľ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚Ē§  
 ‚Ēā N+1 queries ‚Ēā List views with relationships must use ->with() eager loading ‚Ēā Performance ‚ÄĒ a list of 50 records making 50 extra ‚Ēā  
 ‚Ēā ‚Ēā ‚Ēā queries ‚Ēā  
 ‚Ēú‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚Ēľ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚Ēľ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚Ē§  
 ‚Ēā Dead code ‚Ēā No empty methods, no 5+ line comment blocks, no unused use ‚Ēā Code bloat, confusion for next developer ‚Ēā
‚Ēā ‚Ēā imports ‚Ēā ‚Ēā  
 ‚ĒĒ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚Ēī‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚Ēī‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚Ēė

4. Adversarial Security (Stage 6 ‚ÄĒ REVIEW via curl)

This is the stage that was broken before. Now requires actual exploitation attempts against the running dev server:

‚ĒĆ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚Ē¨‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚Ē¨‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚Ēź  
 ‚Ēā Attack ‚Ēā Method ‚Ēā Pass criteria ‚Ēā
‚Ēú‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚Ēľ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚Ēľ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚Ē§
‚Ēā Cross-home record access ‚Ēā curl with record ID from different home ‚Ēā 404, not the data ‚Ēā
‚Ēú‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚Ēľ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚Ēľ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚Ē§
‚Ēā Cross-home FK injection ‚Ēā curl create/update with FK from different home ‚Ēā Rejected, not created ‚Ēā  
 ‚Ēú‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚Ēľ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚Ēľ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚Ē§  
 ‚Ēā Cross-home source record ‚Ēā curl create-from-X with source from different home ‚Ēā Rejected ‚Ēā  
 ‚Ēú‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚Ēľ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚Ēľ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚Ē§

‚Ēú‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚Ēľ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚Ēľ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚Ē§

‚Ēú‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚Ēľ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚Ēľ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚Ē§

 ‚ĒĒ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚Ēī‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚Ēī‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚Ēė

6e. Manual Test Checklist ‚ÄĒ verified by user in browser

This is the new hard gate. Before PUSH, the workflow prints:

‚ēĒ‚ēź‚ēź‚ēź‚ēź‚ēź‚ēź‚ēź‚ēź‚ēź‚ēź‚ēź‚ēź‚ēź‚ēź‚ēź‚ēź‚ēź‚ēź‚ēź‚ēź‚ēź‚ēź‚ēź‚ēź‚ēź‚ēź‚ēź‚ēź‚ēź‚ēź‚ēź‚ēź‚ēź‚ēź‚ēź‚ēź‚ēź‚ēź‚ēź‚ēź‚ēź‚ēź‚ēź‚ēź‚ēź‚ēź‚ēź‚ēź‚ēź‚ēź‚ēź‚ēź‚ēź‚ēź‚ēź‚ēź‚ēź‚ēź‚ēź‚ēź‚ēź‚ēź‚ēó  
 ‚ēĎ MANUAL TEST CHECKLIST ‚ÄĒ [Feature Name] ‚ēĎ
‚ē†‚ēź‚ēź‚ēź‚ēź‚ēź‚ēź‚ēź‚ēź‚ēź‚ēź‚ēź‚ēź‚ēź‚ēź‚ēź‚ēź‚ēź‚ēź‚ēź‚ēź‚ēź‚ēź‚ēź‚ēź‚ēź‚ēź‚ēź‚ēź‚ēź‚ēź‚ēź‚ēź‚ēź‚ēź‚ēź‚ēź‚ēź‚ēź‚ēź‚ēź‚ēź‚ēź‚ēź‚ēź‚ēź‚ēź‚ēź‚ēź‚ēź‚ēź‚ēź‚ēź‚ēź‚ēź‚ēź‚ēź‚ēź‚ēź‚ēź‚ēź‚ēź‚ēź‚ē£

‚ēĎ ‚Ė° Create a record ‚Üí verify it appears ‚ēĎ

 ‚ēĎ Reply "tested" or report bugs. ‚ēĎ  
 ‚ēö‚ēź‚ēź‚ēź‚ēź‚ēź‚ēź‚ēź‚ēź‚ēź‚ēź‚ēź‚ēź‚ēź‚ēź‚ēź‚ēź‚ēź‚ēź‚ēź‚ēź‚ēź‚ēź‚ēź‚ēź‚ēź‚ēź‚ēź‚ēź‚ēź‚ēź‚ēź‚ēź‚ēź‚ēź‚ēź‚ēź‚ēź‚ēź‚ēź‚ēź‚ēź‚ēź‚ēź‚ēź‚ēź‚ēź‚ēź‚ēź‚ēź‚ēź‚ēź‚ēź‚ēź‚ēź‚ēź‚ēź‚ēź‚ēź‚ēź‚ēź‚ēź‚ēź‚ēĚ

PUSH is blocked until you confirm "tested". This catches the things I can't test ‚ÄĒ the Body Maps color persistence bug, the modal chaining, the  
 date picker initialization, the Select2 dropdowns. Those are browser-only issues.

 ‚Ēā Browser testing only happened when you manually found bugs ‚Ēā Browser testing is a mandatory gate with a printed checklist ‚Ēā

 ‚Ēā Security audit was a separate step you had to ask for ‚Ēā Security is baked into REVIEW ‚ÄĒ no separate ask needed ‚Ēā
‚Ēú‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚Ēľ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚Ē§  
 ‚Ēā "PASS" meant "the code looks right" ‚Ēā "PASS" means "the attack failed" or "the curl returned what we expected" ‚Ēā
‚ĒĒ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚Ēī‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚Ēė

The workflow now produces production-ready code by default. You shouldn't need to ask "is this secure?" or "is this production ready?" again ‚ÄĒ if
it passes the pipeline, it's been attacked, verified, and browser-tested.

‚úĽ Cooked for 56s
